Elemental Bodies: Eternal Aspects
Explanation of the eternal aspects of elemental bodies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand which aspects of elemental bodies are considered eternal in the Aristotelian framework.

Core Idea
Elemental bodies are eternal in matter, corporeal form by type, and specific forms by genus.

The author now turns to elemental (earthly) bodies. He explains that they are eternal in three respects: their matter, their corporeal form (as a type that persists through individuals), and their specific forms (as a genus that persists through various species). This lesson focuses on these eternal dimensions and the reasoning behind them.

Guided Path
1
Read the elemental bodies passage
Read from 'وأما العنصريات' up to 'بتعاقب أنواعه'.
This covers the eternal aspects of elemental bodies.
2
Identify the three eternal aspects
The passage lists matter, corporeal form by type, and specific forms by genus. Note the distinct ways each is eternal.
Corporeal form is a single type; specific forms share a genus.
3
Understand the reasoning
For corporeal form: matter is never devoid of it, and its type persists through individuals. For specific forms: matter must always have one, and their genus persists through types.
The continuity is through succession, not individual permanence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني : إنها قديمة بذواتها وصفاتها وإليه ذهب أرسطو ومن تبعه من متأخري الفلاسفة كالفارابي وابن سينا، وتفصيل مذهبهم أنهم قالوا : الأجسام تنقسم كما علمت إلى فلكيات وعنصريات، أما الفلكيات فإنها قديمة بموادها وصورها الجسمية والنوعية ( وأعراضها ( المعينة من المقادير والأشكال وغيرها ) إلا الحركات والأوضاع المشخصة فإنها حادثة ) قطعاً ضرورة أن كل حركة شخصية مسبوقة بأخرى لا إلى نهاية وكذا الأوضاع المعينة التابعة لها، وأما مطلق الحركة والوضع فقديم أيضاً لأن مذهبهم أن الأفلاك متحركة مستمرة من الأزل إلى الأبد بلا سكون أصلاً . ( وأما العنصريات فقديمة بموادها وبصورها الجسمية (بنوعها وذلك لأن المادة لا تخلو عن الصورة الجسمية التي هي طبيعة واحدة نوعية لا تختلف إلا بأمور خارجة عن حقيقتها فيكون نوعها مستمر الوجود بتعاقب أفرادها أزلاً وأبداً ، ) وبصورها النوعية بجنسها ) وذلك لأن مادتها لا يجوز خلوها عن صورها النوعية بأسرها بل لا بد أن يكون معها واحدة منها لكن هذه الصور متشاركة في جنسها دون ماهيتها النوعية فيكون جنسها مستمر الوجود بتعاقب أنواعه (نعم) الصور المشخصة فيهما أي في الصورة الجسمية والنوعية ( والأعراض المختصة ( المعينة ( محدثة ولا امتناع في حدوث بعض الصور النوعية ) العنصرية كأن يكون مثلاً نوع الإنسان حادثاً غير مستمر الوجود تتعاقب أفراده الشخصية، إذ يجوز حصوله من عنصر آخر بطريق الكون والفساد ولا امتناع أيضاً عندهم في استمراره كذلك ولا في استمرار أنواع المركبات في ضمن أفرادها المتعاقبة بلا نهاية
The second: They are eternal in their essences and attributes, and to it went Aristotle and those who followed him among the later philosophers, like al-Fārābī and Ibn Sīnā. The detail of their doctrine is that they said: Bodies are divided, as you have learned, into celestial and elemental. As for celestial bodies, they are eternal in their matters, their corporeal and specific forms, and their determinate accidents – quantities, shapes, and others – except for the individual motions and positions, for they are originated, necessarily, because every individual motion is preceded by another ad infinitum, and likewise the determinate positions dependent on them. As for absolute motion and position, they are also eternal, because their doctrine is that the celestial spheres are in continuous motion from eternity to eternity without any rest at all. As for elemental bodies, they are eternal in their matters and in their corporeal forms by their type, because matter is never devoid of the corporeal form, which is a single nature of a type that does not differ except by matters external to its reality; so its type is continuously existent through the succession of its individuals eternally and forever; and in their specific forms by their genus, because their matter cannot be devoid of all their specific forms, but rather must have one of them with it. However, these forms share in their genus but not in their specific quiddity; so their genus is continuously existent through the succession of its types. Indeed, the individualizing forms in both – that is, in the corporeal and specific forms – and the specific determinate accidents are originated. There is no impossibility in the origination of some elemental specific forms, such as for example the human type being originated, not continuously existent, with its personal individuals succeeding one another, for it is possible that it arises from another element by way of generation and corruption. And there is also no impossibility in their view in its continuation thus, nor in the continuation of the types of compounds within their successive individuals ad infinitum.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage presents the second division of bodies – that they are eternal in both essence and attributes. The author attributes this view to Aristotle and his later followers, al-Fārābī and Ibn Sīnā. The exposition then provides a detailed breakdown of the philosophers' position by dividing bodies into celestial (falakiyyāt) and elemental (ʿunṣuriyyāt). For celestial bodies, they are eternal in matter, corporeal form, specific form, and determinate accidents (quantities, shapes, etc.) – except for individual motions (ḥarakāt shakhṣiyya) and positions (awḍāʿ), which are originated. The reason given is that each individual motion is preceded by another to infinity, so there cannot be a first motion. However, motion in the absolute sense (muṭlaq al-ḥaraka) and position (al-waḍʿ) are eternal because the celestial spheres move continuously from pre‑eternity to post‑eternity without ever ceasing. For elemental bodies, the philosophers hold them eternal in matter and in corporeal form by type (bi‑nawʿihā), because matter always has a corporeal form of a single type, and the type persists through successive individuals. They are also eternal in specific forms by genus (bi‑jinsihā), because matter must always have some specific form, and these specific forms share a genus that persists through successive types. However, the individualizing forms (al-ṣuwar al-mushakhkhiṣa) in both corporeal and specific forms, as well as the determinate accidents, are originated. The author adds that there is no contradiction in the view that some elemental specific forms (like the human type) may be originated and not continuously existent, as they could arise from another element via generation and corruption. Similarly, the continuation of such types or the types of compounds within successive individuals ad infinitum is possible in their doctrine. This detailed exposition clarifies the nuanced stance of the Peripatetic philosophers.

Key Terms
عنصريات
صورة جسمية
صورة نوعية
جنس
نوع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that elemental bodies are eternal in all aspects, including individual forms.
Correction: Only matter, corporeal form by type, and specific forms by genus are eternal; individual forms and accidents are originated.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how is the corporeal form of elemental bodies eternal?
A) Each individual corporeal form is eternal.
B) The type of corporeal form persists through successive individuals.
C) The genus of corporeal form persists through successive types.
D) Corporeal form is not eternal.

Key Takeaway
Elemental bodies are eternal in matter, in the type of corporeal form, and in the genus of specific forms.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your physical body is just a temporary individual in a long chain of the same type, how should that change the way you care for your body and how you view its eventual decay? What does this say about your personal identity beyond the physical?
?
The passage says matter always has some specific form; you never encounter formless matter. Does that make you more aware of the order and purpose in every material thing? How can you train yourself to see the Creator's design in the ordinary objects around you?
?
If the genus of specific forms persists eternally, then every material thing has a necessary continuity. Does that comfort you or unnerve you? How does this affect your belief in the Hereafter, where the material world will be replaced? Will you live today as if this world's forms are temporary or eternal?

Elemental Bodies: Originated Aspects and Possibilities
Explanation of originated aspects and the possibility of originated specific types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand which aspects of elemental bodies are originated and the possibility of originated specific types like humans.

Core Idea
Individual forms and accidents are originated, and even some specific types may be originated.

After discussing what is eternal in elemental bodies, the author turns to what is originated. He states that individualizing forms and determinate accidents are originated. Moreover, he notes that it is possible for some specific forms (like the human type) to be originated and to persist through successive individuals, a view compatible with the Aristotelian framework.

Guided Path
1
Read the final section
Read from 'نعم الصور المشخصة' to the end of the passage.
This covers originated aspects and the possibility of originated types.
2
Identify originated aspects
The passage mentions individualizing forms in both corporeal and specific forms, as well as determinate accidents, as originated.
These are the changing particulars.
3
Understand the possibility of originated types
The author says there is no impossibility in some specific forms (e.g., human) being originated and then continuing through individuals.
This shows flexibility in the doctrine.
4
Note the implication
The passage concludes that the continuation of types and compounds ad infinitum is also possible.
This aligns with the idea of eternal succession.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني : إنها قديمة بذواتها وصفاتها وإليه ذهب أرسطو ومن تبعه من متأخري الفلاسفة كالفارابي وابن سينا، وتفصيل مذهبهم أنهم قالوا : الأجسام تنقسم كما علمت إلى فلكيات وعنصريات، أما الفلكيات فإنها قديمة بموادها وصورها الجسمية والنوعية ( وأعراضها ( المعينة من المقادير والأشكال وغيرها ) إلا الحركات والأوضاع المشخصة فإنها حادثة ) قطعاً ضرورة أن كل حركة شخصية مسبوقة بأخرى لا إلى نهاية وكذا الأوضاع المعينة التابعة لها، وأما مطلق الحركة والوضع فقديم أيضاً لأن مذهبهم أن الأفلاك متحركة مستمرة من الأزل إلى الأبد بلا سكون أصلاً . ( وأما العنصريات فقديمة بموادها وبصورها الجسمية (بنوعها وذلك لأن المادة لا تخلو عن الصورة الجسمية التي هي طبيعة واحدة نوعية لا تختلف إلا بأمور خارجة عن حقيقتها فيكون نوعها مستمر الوجود بتعاقب أفرادها أزلاً وأبداً ، ) وبصورها النوعية بجنسها ) وذلك لأن مادتها لا يجوز خلوها عن صورها النوعية بأسرها بل لا بد أن يكون معها واحدة منها لكن هذه الصور متشاركة في جنسها دون ماهيتها النوعية فيكون جنسها مستمر الوجود بتعاقب أنواعه (نعم) الصور المشخصة فيهما أي في الصورة الجسمية والنوعية ( والأعراض المختصة ( المعينة ( محدثة ولا امتناع في حدوث بعض الصور النوعية ) العنصرية كأن يكون مثلاً نوع الإنسان حادثاً غير مستمر الوجود تتعاقب أفراده الشخصية، إذ يجوز حصوله من عنصر آخر بطريق الكون والفساد ولا امتناع أيضاً عندهم في استمراره كذلك ولا في استمرار أنواع المركبات في ضمن أفرادها المتعاقبة بلا نهاية
The second: They are eternal in their essences and attributes, and to it went Aristotle and those who followed him among the later philosophers, like al-Fārābī and Ibn Sīnā. The detail of their doctrine is that they said: Bodies are divided, as you have learned, into celestial and elemental. As for celestial bodies, they are eternal in their matters, their corporeal and specific forms, and their determinate accidents – quantities, shapes, and others – except for the individual motions and positions, for they are originated, necessarily, because every individual motion is preceded by another ad infinitum, and likewise the determinate positions dependent on them. As for absolute motion and position, they are also eternal, because their doctrine is that the celestial spheres are in continuous motion from eternity to eternity without any rest at all. As for elemental bodies, they are eternal in their matters and in their corporeal forms by their type, because matter is never devoid of the corporeal form, which is a single nature of a type that does not differ except by matters external to its reality; so its type is continuously existent through the succession of its individuals eternally and forever; and in their specific forms by their genus, because their matter cannot be devoid of all their specific forms, but rather must have one of them with it. However, these forms share in their genus but not in their specific quiddity; so their genus is continuously existent through the succession of its types. Indeed, the individualizing forms in both – that is, in the corporeal and specific forms – and the specific determinate accidents are originated. There is no impossibility in the origination of some elemental specific forms, such as for example the human type being originated, not continuously existent, with its personal individuals succeeding one another, for it is possible that it arises from another element by way of generation and corruption. And there is also no impossibility in their view in its continuation thus, nor in the continuation of the types of compounds within their successive individuals ad infinitum.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage presents the second division of bodies – that they are eternal in both essence and attributes. The author attributes this view to Aristotle and his later followers, al-Fārābī and Ibn Sīnā. The exposition then provides a detailed breakdown of the philosophers' position by dividing bodies into celestial (falakiyyāt) and elemental (ʿunṣuriyyāt). For celestial bodies, they are eternal in matter, corporeal form, specific form, and determinate accidents (quantities, shapes, etc.) – except for individual motions (ḥarakāt shakhṣiyya) and positions (awḍāʿ), which are originated. The reason given is that each individual motion is preceded by another to infinity, so there cannot be a first motion. However, motion in the absolute sense (muṭlaq al-ḥaraka) and position (al-waḍʿ) are eternal because the celestial spheres move continuously from pre‑eternity to post‑eternity without ever ceasing. For elemental bodies, the philosophers hold them eternal in matter and in corporeal form by type (bi‑nawʿihā), because matter always has a corporeal form of a single type, and the type persists through successive individuals. They are also eternal in specific forms by genus (bi‑jinsihā), because matter must always have some specific form, and these specific forms share a genus that persists through successive types. However, the individualizing forms (al-ṣuwar al-mushakhkhiṣa) in both corporeal and specific forms, as well as the determinate accidents, are originated. The author adds that there is no contradiction in the view that some elemental specific forms (like the human type) may be originated and not continuously existent, as they could arise from another element via generation and corruption. Similarly, the continuation of such types or the types of compounds within successive individuals ad infinitum is possible in their doctrine. This detailed exposition clarifies the nuanced stance of the Peripatetic philosophers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the Aristotelians believe every species of elemental bodies is eternal without any origination.
Correction: The passage explicitly says that some specific forms like the human type may be originated.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is said about the human type?
A) It is eternal and never originated.
B) It is possible for it to be originated and then continue.
C) It is impossible for it to be originated.
D) It is originated but cannot continue.

Key Takeaway
Individual forms and accidents are originated, and some species may be originated while the overall succession continues eternally.

Allah's Existence

The Impossibility of Eternal Individualizing Forms
Commentator argues against eternal individualizing forms using infinite regress.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why individualizing forms cannot be eternal by their type or genus, due to the logical problem of infinite regress.

Core Idea
Eternal individualizing forms lead to an infinite regress, which is impossible.

In this passage, the commentator explains a key point that is often misunderstood: how can specific forms be eternal? He argues that if an individualizing form were eternal by its type or genus, it would require another form to individualize it, and so on indefinitely. This sets the stage for understanding the limits of eternity in physical forms.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
Read the passage and find the statement about the impossibility of individualizing forms being eternal by type or genus. Notice the reasoning: if they were eternal, they would need further individualization.
2
Understand the infinite regress
Trace the logical chain: each individualizing form would require another individualizing form, leading to an infinite sequence (tasalsul). Why is this problematic in Islamic theology?
3
Contrast with the alternative
The commentator mentions that the only conceivable way for such a form to be eternal is by a 'general accident' (al-ʿaraḍ al-ʿāmm), but he dismisses this as meaningless. Reflect on why that is not a satisfactory solution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (نعم الصور المشخصة فيهما هذا من تتمة قوله : أنهم قالوا إلخ ولا يذهب عليك ) أن الصورة المشخصة لا يتصور أن يكون قديمة بنوعها أو بجنسها وإلا لكانت محتاجة إلى صورة أخرى مشخصة أو منوعة وهلم جراً فيلزم التسلسل وإنما المتصور هو أن يكون قديمة بالعرض العام ولا عبرة بذلك . قوله : ( كأن يكون نوع الإنسان حادثاً مع أن نوع الإنسان كان قديماً عندهم وأن امتزاجه كانت مركبة من العناصر الأربعة فيلزم أن يكون نوعاً النار في ضمن تلك الأفراد قديماً عندهم، هذا ولعلهم أرادوا بحدوثه حدوث كرة النار بحركات الأفلاك بطريق الكون والفساد وأن هذه الكرة مخالفة بالنوع للأجزاء النارية التي في المركبات أو ردوا بقولهم : وبصروها النوعية بجنسها أن المقطوع عندهم هو أن يكون الصور النوعية للعنصريات قديمة بجنسها لا أن يكون قديمة بأنواعها على ما يشعر به قول (المصنف) ولا امتناع في حدوثه إلخ. وكذا قول الشارح: ولا امتناع أيضاً عندهم .
His statement: 'Indeed, the individualizing forms in both' – this is part of the completion of his statement that they said etc. And let it not be hidden from you that the individualizing form cannot be conceived to be eternal by its type or by its genus, for otherwise it would need another individualizing or specific form, and so on, leading to an infinite regress. What can be conceived is that it is eternal by a general accident (al-ʿaraḍ al-ʿāmm), and no attention is paid to that. His statement: 'As for example the human type being originated' – even though the human type was eternal in their view, and its mixture was composed of the four elements, it would follow that the type of fire within those individuals would be eternal in their view. This – and perhaps they intended by its origination the origination of the sphere of fire by the motions of the celestial spheres through generation and corruption, and that this sphere is different in type from the fiery parts in compounds. Or they rejected by their statement: 'and their specific forms by their genus' that what is certain in their view is that the specific forms of elemental bodies are eternal by their genus, not that they are eternal by their types, as indicated by the statement of the author: 'and there is no impossibility in its origination' etc. Similarly the statement of the commentator: 'and there is also no impossibility in their view.'
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage contains two comments (qālahu) from the commentator on the main text. The first comment explains the phrase 'indeed, the individualizing forms in both' from the earlier discussion of celestial and elemental bodies. The commentator clarifies that an individualizing form (ṣūra mushakhkhiṣa) cannot be eternal by its type (nawʿ) or genus (jins), because that would require an infinite regress of further individualizing forms. The only conceivable way for such a form to be eternal is by a general accident (al-ʿaraḍ al-ʿāmm), but that is not meaningful. The second comment addresses the example of the human type being originated. The commentator notes that if the human type were originated, it might seem to contradict the philosophers' view that the human type is eternal. He explains that the philosophers may mean by 'origination' the origination of the sphere of fire (kurat al-nār) through celestial motions via generation and corruption, which is a different type from the fire particles in compounds. Alternatively, the philosophers' statement that 'their specific forms by their genus' indicates that elemental specific forms are eternal by genus, not by individual types, so a new type like human could originate within that genus without contradicting the principle of eternal generic forms. The commentator concludes by noting that the author and the commentator both assert that there is no impossibility in such origination.

Key Terms
الصور المشخصة
التسلسل
العرض العام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Individualizing forms can be eternal in themselves without any further cause.
Correction: If a form were eternal by its own type, it would still require individualization, leading to an infinite regress, which is impossible. Thus such forms cannot be eternal.

Checkpoint
Why can an individualizing form not be eternal by its type or genus?
A) Because it would be too complex
B) Because it would require an infinite regress of forms
C) Because the author said so
D) Because it contradicts the Torah

Key Takeaway
Individualizing forms cannot be eternal by type or genus because that leads to an infinite regress, which is rationally impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider the infinite regress argument, ask yourself: in what areas of your own life do you rely on an endless chain of justifications (e.g., 'I'll pray later when I'm less busy, and later when that's less busy...') rather than stopping at a firm foundation? What is that foundation for you?
?
This passage shows that some things cannot be pushed back infinitely. Is there a belief or habit in your relationship with Allah that you have been postponing indefinitely, assuming it will somehow resolve itself? What concrete step will you take today to end that regression?
?
The commentator dismisses the idea of eternity by a general accident as irrelevant. Are there 'general accidents' in your daily life—things you treat as important but are really just distractions from what is essential? How can you refocus on what truly matters for your akhira?
